  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9d16553c-a572-4923-883f-7a82d6746190'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_189416339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189416339" />
    <a title="Judah Nielsen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5878974-judah-nielsen"><img alt="Judah Nielsen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370495308p2/5878974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189416339?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judah Nielsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judah Nielsen" href="/user/show/5878974-judah-nielsen">Judah Nielsen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5878974-judah-nielsen?shelf=fluff">fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5878974-judah-nielsen?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5878974-judah-nielsen?shelf=sf-f">sf-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5878974-judah-nielsen?shelf=1900-1999">1900-1999</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189416339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13529453632970595907">So, this is the second book of a trilogy, and then there's another trilogy, and then some other books, and when you've tallied it all up, you have something like 27 books in the series. And I've read the first two, but unless I get pneumonia and my reading time suddenly quadruples, I'm probably done, and I feel strange about it, because when all is said and done, I don't hate these books.<br/><br/>The setting is imaginative. The stories move along at a good pace. The stories are interesting. If that was a</span>
  <span id="freeText13529453632970595907" style="display:none">So, this is the second book of a trilogy, and then there's another trilogy, and then some other books, and when you've tallied it all up, you have something like 27 books in the series. And I've read the first two, but unless I get pneumonia and my reading time suddenly quadruples, I'm probably done, and I feel strange about it, because when all is said and done, I don't hate these books.<br /><br />The setting is imaginative. The stories move along at a good pace. The stories are interesting. If that was all their was to a book, this would be a pretty decent read. <br /><br />But it isn't.<br /><br />The characters are garbage. They're cardboard. The heroes never make any mistakes, but they also never do anything interesting. If anything they do is surprising, it isn't genuinely surprising, it just wasn't foreshadowed.<br /><br />The writing, the style? Also largely nonsense. When I got to the end of the book, and I found myself wondering what happened in the next one, I had a flash of inspiration: I would much rather read the plot summary than the actual plot. <br /><br />What I like about this series is the hierarchy, the relationships between people, the structure of the world, and how the events in the story impact that society. But since I don't like or care about any of the individual people, it's more than enough to just read what happened next, in bullet points or on a timeline.<br /><br />So fuck it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13529453632970595907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3595567763" />
    <a title="Cathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/978552-cathy"><img alt="Cathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604572841p2/978552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3595567763?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/978552-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/978552-cathy?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3595567763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17631933778551696030">My first re-read since being a young adult. I went into Dragonquest with slight apprehension. I never much liked the drama with the Oldtimers and Kylara always grated. But we also get fire-lizards! Love them! Want one! I didn‘t remember that they show up for the first time in Dragonquest. My memory had placed them securely with Menolly and the Harperhall trilogy...<br/><br/>The language feels a little dated sometimes, however that feeling disappeared as I delved deeper into the story. <br/><br/>The gender roles are</span>
  <span id="freeText17631933778551696030" style="display:none">My first re-read since being a young adult. I went into Dragonquest with slight apprehension. I never much liked the drama with the Oldtimers and Kylara always grated. But we also get fire-lizards! Love them! Want one! I didn‘t remember that they show up for the first time in Dragonquest. My memory had placed them securely with Menolly and the Harperhall trilogy...<br /><br />The language feels a little dated sometimes, however that feeling disappeared as I delved deeper into the story. <br /><br />The gender roles are old-fashioned. But I think that is largely on purpose and there are some indications that it could or should be different. There are some hints at non-normative pairings, because what do you do when you ride a green dragon, right?<br /><br />Characters in general are not explored much emotionally. The developing romance between Brekke and F‘nor delves a little deeper and I enjoyed that part. Writing sex scenes is not something that McCaffrey did well, even for the non-graphic variety.<br /><br />The dragons feel more real to me than they appeared to be in my memory, with more pronounced personalities and intelligence. <br /><br />In this one they find some more ancient tech. As a teenager I found that confusing. And now I find it surprising that they just grab any old tech they find and use it. As if it was perfectly normal to live in a quasi feudal, medieval society, find a microscope or a telescope, figure out how works and just use it. If they regressed in their technological level, wouldn‘t that rather be like magic and very unsettling for them? How can they be at the level they are and then back-engineer electrical wiring, etc.? <br /><br />Anyway, I ended up enjoying this book very much, more than Dragonflight. Onwards to The White Dragon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17631933778551696030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187497092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187497092" />
    <a title="Jerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry"><img alt="Jerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520438201p2/5855981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187497092?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerry" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry">Jerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187497092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15821557989468356583">In my review of <i>Dragonflight</i>, I compared that starter <i>Pern</i> novel to a series premiere of a television show; although it was a bit rough around the edges, it showed some signs of promise. <i>Dragonquest</i>, although still not perfect, was an improvement over its prequel. The story was just as good, and the writing was better. Now, I just hope that the upswing continues throughout the rest of the <i>Pern</i> series, as long as it is.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780345453969" href="/book/show/7033634-dragonquest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116652-punk?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116652-punk?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189537593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16865351932112549262">Fantasy. Again, this book teaches that the way to a woman's heart is through dubious consent. This time it's just F'nor being a dick; horny telepathic dragons had nothing to do with it. Apparently our hero sees nothing wrong with having sex with a woman who is "fighting him." He's also a big fan of domestic violence: "It was too bad you couldn't beat a Weyrwoman with impunity. Her dragon wouldn't permit it but a sound thrashing was what Kylara badly needed."<br/><br/>Look, I didn't like Kylara either. <i>No </i></span>
  <span id="freeText16865351932112549262" style="display:none">Fantasy. Again, this book teaches that the way to a woman's heart is through dubious consent. This time it's just F'nor being a dick; horny telepathic dragons had nothing to do with it. Apparently our hero sees nothing wrong with having sex with a woman who is "fighting him." He's also a big fan of domestic violence: "It was too bad you couldn't beat a Weyrwoman with impunity. Her dragon wouldn't permit it but a sound thrashing was what Kylara badly needed."<br /><br />Look, I didn't like Kylara either. <i>No one likes Kylara</i> because McCaffrey didn't want us to like her. The woman is extremely unsympathetic. But oh my god that does not make it okay for the hero to want to beat her. Ugh, Anne McCaffrey, Your Issues.<br /><br />Despite Anne McCaffrey's issues, which I knew about going into this, I like this world enough to keep reading until she really pisses me off. In this book she addresses the tension between the modern and the old weyrs. They have different ways of managing their societies and of course those ways clash so there's some political maneuvering and palace intrigue type stuff while F'lar tries to rule all of Pern.<br /><br />Three stars. I liked this one for the science, the problem-solving, and the fire lizards. The plot's pretty engaging too, when it isn't broken up by pointless rambling.<br /><br />eBook: Lots of OCR errors and the section breaks aren't marked; still it was in better shape than Dragonflight, which is funny because I actually read these two as an omnibus.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3474928118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3474928118" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3474928118?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3474928118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7004482799643151525">I'm not sure why I never read these as a teenager, but I sure am enjoying them now. The writing has an unselfconscious quaintness and ease that is quite endearing. The story easily positions itself as a kind of science fantasy hybrid without even trying to align wholly on one end or the other of the speculative fiction spectrum. <br/><br/>The characters are all much more fleshed out than they were in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern___1_' title='Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonflight</a>, and the story has a smoother and well paced progression. I am enjoying the mix of politics a</span>
  <span id="freeText7004482799643151525" style="display:none">I'm not sure why I never read these as a teenager, but I sure am enjoying them now. The writing has an unselfconscious quaintness and ease that is quite endearing. The story easily positions itself as a kind of science fantasy hybrid without even trying to align wholly on one end or the other of the speculative fiction spectrum. <br /><br />The characters are all much more fleshed out than they were in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern___1_" title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a>, and the story has a smoother and well paced progression. I am enjoying the mix of politics and action that arises with conflict between Craft, Holder, and Weyr; and the extent to which they put aside (or don't) their differences in the effort to fight the shared threat of Thread. The tension between the Oldtimer riders and Benden Weyr is actually quite frustrating, but at the same time, has the unfortunate ring of truth.<br /><br />The individual characters are a realistic mix of likeable to horrible, with varying degrees of competence arrayed among them. I never tired of reading about whoever the story followed at any given time.<br /><br />The dragons are amazing, but I wish we actually had a dragon POV as they are such interesting creatures. The fire-lizards seem like they are even more than they appear, and I hope to see more of them!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7004482799643151525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7293924181598744618">Fantastic. I am able to just immerse myself into this world. I can feel like I belong there. The characters are fantastically written and I feel myself becoming attached to them. There are also some that I just despise. I love this world that McCaffrey created. I love the history of it, but these books that I am reading now are at the heart of the world and what I loved about Pern. <br/><br/>This has been such a great reread.   <span id="freeText7293924181598744618" style="display:none">Fantastic. I am able to just immerse myself into this world. I can feel like I belong there. The characters are fantastically written and I feel myself becoming attached to them. There are also some that I just despise. I love this world that McCaffrey created. I love the history of it, but these books that I am reading now are at the heart of the world and what I loved about Pern. <br /><br />This has been such a great reread. I am thoroughly enjoying reliving all of these events that were so long forgotten. So much goes on that it is hard to summarize. It is definitely not boring. There is always something happening. There is love and tragedy and perseverance. Great series to read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16249521784168802568">Well, we found out dragons can travel in time as well as space, and people from the past don't get along well with people in the present...</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630103582?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RJ from the LBC" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc">RJ from the LBC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780722159040" href="/book/show/2331485.Dragonquest">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630103582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10059268093141561136">The ongoing saga of a distant future offworld colony where society and technology have regressed to feudal times yet men (and a few women) ride genetically engineered, teleporting, time-traveling, telepathic dragons in order to protect their homelands from the menacing threat of destructive intergalactic, uh, thread. The writing is an improvement over the first installment which was an uneven mashup of two novellas, although the story this time is really just an episodic continuation of the firs</span>
  <span id="freeText10059268093141561136" style="display:none">The ongoing saga of a distant future offworld colony where society and technology have regressed to feudal times yet men (and a few women) ride genetically engineered, teleporting, time-traveling, telepathic dragons in order to protect their homelands from the menacing threat of destructive intergalactic, uh, thread. The writing is an improvement over the first installment which was an uneven mashup of two novellas, although the story this time is really just an episodic continuation of the first book with a focus on clarifying aspects of the society and culture and expanding the world of Pern rather than on boring, unimportant things like character arcs or plot. Published almost 50 years ago, the book certainly shows its age with women in traditional and subservient roles for the most part, cooking and cleaning and waiting around for a man to take interest in them, although consent doesn't necessarily play a big part in relationships apparently. And although some of the action moments can be gloriously fun, it's mystifying why the majority of the book focuses instead on romantic swooning and political bickering. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10059268093141561136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_394439860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/394439860" />
    <a title="Kerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/382536-kerry"><img alt="Kerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241083653p2/382536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/394439860?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry" href="/user/show/382536-kerry">Kerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780345453969" href="/book/show/7033634-dragonquest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=8">8</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer394439860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10207445060432463527">I've always liked this book in the Pern series, probably more than I like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Pern___1_' title='Dragonflight (Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonflight</a>. I really like F'nor and Brekke and the introduction of the fire lizards. It's also in this book that the characters really start to begin discovering their history and the technology of the Ancients, which is a trope I generally always really like in SF/Fantasy. I love those cross-over books that feel like fantasy but you discover have a solid, SF premise underneath.<br/><br/>I absorbed the Pern books so long ago in my</span>
  <span id="freeText10207445060432463527" style="display:none">I've always liked this book in the Pern series, probably more than I like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Pern___1_" title="Dragonflight (Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a>. I really like F'nor and Brekke and the introduction of the fire lizards. It's also in this book that the characters really start to begin discovering their history and the technology of the Ancients, which is a trope I generally always really like in SF/Fantasy. I love those cross-over books that feel like fantasy but you discover have a solid, SF premise underneath.<br /><br />I absorbed the Pern books so long ago in my reading life (they were some of my first SFF, loaned to me by one of my father's PhD students; she was my book provider for a long time in my teens) that I don't think I've ever really watched the progress of the story McCaffrey unfolded.<br /><br />I remember I got a delightful surprise with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Pern___5_" title="The White Dragon (Pern, #5) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">The White Dragon</a> and later <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/465904.Dragonsdawn__Pern___9_" title="Dragonsdawn (Pern, #9) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsdawn</a> as we really began to discover the Ancients (oh, how I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46590.The_Goddess_in_Every_Girl_Develop_Your_Teen_Feminine_Power" title="The Goddess in Every Girl Develop Your Teen Feminine Power by M.J. Abadie" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsdawn</a> when it came out). Looking back now, with much older eyes, and reading the books in sequence, I can see that McCaffrey must have had the basic idea for the Ninth and First Passes from the beginning. The first setup came in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Pern___1_" title="Dragonflight (Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a>, but that book was too full of world building, character introduction and the beginning of Threadfall for much to be done with it. Here, it starts in earnest. I ate it up way back then, and I admit, I'm eating it up all over again.<br /><br />This book was originally published in 1971 and it mostly holds up. But, ouch, there are a few misogynistic moments that made me cringe.<br /><br /><i>This was a matter for men to settle,</i> F'lar thinks at one point, although at least he'd been thinking Lessa might be helpful the moment before.<br /><br />Later, someone (F'lar again I think but my quote doesn't include who was thinking it) reflects <i>It was too bad you couldn't beat a Weyrwoman with impunity. Her dragon wouldn't permit it, but a sound thrashing was what Kylara badly needed.</i> Well, she badly needed something, but I'm not sure a thrashing was it.<br /><br />Neither attitude is acceptable, and if my son shows an interest in reading these books when he's older, I'll be pointing that out to him. But all the same, I'm going to give the book a general pass for two bad passages written over 40 years ago. (Not ignore them, but not stomp and throw the book either.) I'll encourage him to read them because they are good stories with (generally good) role models both male and female. All the same, it did make me go ouch.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to rereading the rest of the books (and I'm hoping those problematic attitudes pop up less and less as the books' publication dates get closer to today). I'm seriously tempted to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28541.Dragonsong__Pern___3__Harper_Hall___1_" title="Dragonsong (Pern, #3)(Harper Hall, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsong</a> to that 8 year old son I mentioned above, as I think he's more ready for the tale and politics of Menolly and the fire lizards and the Harper Hall right now. However, I'm rereading McCaffrey in publication order, so <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/177945.To_Ride_Pegasus" title="To Ride Pegasus by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">To Ride Pegasus</a> will be my next McCaffrey (and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9359796.Vortex" title="Vortex by Robert Charles Wilson" rel="nofollow noopener">Vortex</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27276.Robert_Charles_Wilson" title="Robert Charles Wilson" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Charles Wilson</a> my next book).<br /><br />Pern and dragons and fire lizards and Thread! It's been a happy trip back down memory lane so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10207445060432463527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1703533050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703533050" />
    <a title="Edward Rathke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5657249-edward-rathke"><img alt="Edward Rathke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442510992p2/5657249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703533050?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Rathke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Rathke" href="/user/show/5657249-edward-rathke">Edward Rathke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703533050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13009768829413963749">These are peculiar books that are beginning to take on an interesting shape.<br/><br/>The first novel is something I would probably describe as misogynistic, classist, and maybe racist (in what it implies about genetic superiority), and for about half of this I was thinking the same thing. It's odd reading a book written by a woman that seems pretty hateful towards women. Not that women can't be misogynists--it's just not what I expect out of a writer who is a woman.<br/><br/>There's at least an implicit argument i</span>
  <span id="freeText13009768829413963749" style="display:none">These are peculiar books that are beginning to take on an interesting shape.<br /><br />The first novel is something I would probably describe as misogynistic, classist, and maybe racist (in what it implies about genetic superiority), and for about half of this I was thinking the same thing. It's odd reading a book written by a woman that seems pretty hateful towards women. Not that women can't be misogynists--it's just not what I expect out of a writer who is a woman.<br /><br />There's at least an implicit argument in these first two novels that men should take control and women should be docile and support their men, while also being sexually loyal to them, despite the fact that this society has done away with that form of sexual morality.<br /><br />Had I not read Dragonsong first (which, chronologically, comes after this one), I probably wouldn't have continued, but Dragonsong is at least much kinder and more supportive of women, and eschews traditional gender roles.<br /><br />But Dragonquest is actually a link between that more traditional, patriarchal, and racist society presented in Dragonflight and the gradually opening up of society in Dragonsong. We see the society change, evolve, become more open. The classism and totalitarianism and misogyny become eroded by new ways of thinking that develop in this novel, which is pretty cool.<br /><br />It gives all of this an interesting shape. We start with traditional fantasy stuff and are becoming more radical with each novel.<br /><br />Anyrate, the novel itself is deeply sociological. More than a quest or an adventure, it's a restructuring of the world around them.<br /><br />Pretty interesting stuff. Aspects and sequences are still troubling, but I think McCaffrey's doing something a bit more revolutionary than I expected. She's thrown us in a world that feels familiarly upsetting and is transforming that world into a more equitable place.<br /><br />It's also worth remembering when these books came out. McCaffrey was the first woman to win a major SF award for one of the novellas that makes up Dragonflight. It was the early 70s, a time when publishing was especially dominated by masculine voices. So she gave us a masculine and muscular world and story to draw us all in. Then, here, she begins subverting that. Dragonsong subverts it further. <br /><br />I'm interested where these first six books lead. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13009768829413963749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review34485729">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_819568509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Rachel (Kalanadi)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17810287-rachel-kalanadi"><img alt="Rachel (Kalanadi)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574017820p2/17810287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/819568509?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (Kalanadi)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (Kalanadi)" href="/user/show/17810287-rachel-kalanadi">Rachel (Kalanadi)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345314482" href="/book/show/1455429.Dragonquest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17810287-rachel-kalanadi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer819568509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15867378644432317091">More satisfying emotionally than Dragonflight. Lots of changes being put in motion. This book is heavily concerned with challenging traditions of all kinds. F'lar and F'nor are definitely the main characters rather than Lessa* and I remain frustrated with some of their actions and views on women.<br/><br/>F'nor's scene with Brekke was the worst part (more not so consensual sex presented as swooningly romantic) but overall less of the stupid underlying misogyny and infantalizing/domination of women by men.</span>
  <span id="freeText15867378644432317091" style="display:none">More satisfying emotionally than Dragonflight. Lots of changes being put in motion. This book is heavily concerned with challenging traditions of all kinds. F'lar and F'nor are definitely the main characters rather than Lessa* and I remain frustrated with some of their actions and views on women.<br /><br />F'nor's scene with Brekke was the worst part (more not so consensual sex presented as swooningly romantic) but overall less of the stupid underlying misogyny and infantalizing/domination of women by men. So, noticeable if slight improvement.<br /><br />I seriously love where the story is going with plans to end Thread's threat over all of Pern...and one of my favorite ideas in sci fi: a "fantasy" low tech world discovering its roots and ancient high tech! Plus, MUCH more of Masterharper Robinton, one of the few instantly likable and GOOD people introduced in these first two books. And who doesn't love Fandarel's brief appearances and passion for technical efficiency?<br /><br /><br /><br />*In fact my major complaint about this book is how Lessa's triumphant solution to saving Pern in Dragonflight is *literally attributed* to F'lar in at least one scene of dialog in Dragonquest. Overall he benefits politically from it and Lessa's role is diminished. She's sidelined in a feminine caretaker / domestic role in Dragonquest while F'lar is blatantly described as having power over the whole planet after what *she* did. It's the definition of "Men get all the credit in history"....</span>
  <a data-text-id="15867378644432317091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5745307889976187488" style="display:none">The second part of the series and this trilogy is the same well written as the first and has the same virtues that made me like it. In this we add some interesting characters and a little more emotion inside the pages and so we have an equally positive result. The problem, however, is that apart from some political power games, our heroes are mainly concerned with issues of... gardening. This of course does not look very exciting. but in the author's hands this gardening becomes equally epic and heroic with battles of more military books and this balances the situation. So this book is an excellent follow-up.</span>

<div id="review_121100792" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121100792" />
    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458107851p2/3947172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121100792?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121100792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4481284070235157688">10/2014 Buddy Reread with Don as we transverse the past to remember what we have forgotten.<br/><br/>Holy Crackerdoodle!<br/><br/>There was a lot going on in this story. No time to breath. F'lar's nonstop strategizing, planning, brooding set everyone on edge in this one. Man's gonna get someone killed trying to guess his intentions and eager to save him from the inherent danger in his machinations. <br/><br/>Pern is still a seething pit of politics and with the acerbating attitudes of the Oldtimers there is major conflict an</span>
  <span id="freeText4481284070235157688" style="display:none">10/2014 Buddy Reread with Don as we transverse the past to remember what we have forgotten.<br /><br />Holy Crackerdoodle!<br /><br />There was a lot going on in this story. No time to breath. F'lar's nonstop strategizing, planning, brooding set everyone on edge in this one. Man's gonna get someone killed trying to guess his intentions and eager to save him from the inherent danger in his machinations. <br /><br />Pern is still a seething pit of politics and with the acerbating attitudes of the Oldtimers there is major conflict and the hard won cooperation is fracturing. Then there's wild matings out of control, hatchings with surprises, new discoveries, and poor F'nor gets the short end of the stick--Again. <br /><br />We finally get our fire lizards and they're as adorable and excitable as I remember. The Southern continent yielded such amazing things and the developments in the Crafthalls are impressive. Always inspiring what intelligent and driven people can accomplish. Fandarel, Robinton, and F'lar are the triumvirate leading Pern into the future. F'lar unique position puts others in the line of fire as they can't endanger him.<br /><br />Of course... there was the knife fight!<br /><br />So if I was there. There'd be three dead bodies and one person smacked around pretty good until they could see sense. A lot of unwarranted forgiveness and deferring problems to the future that does not sit well with me. *huff*<br /><br />Loved the fire lizards. Loved the white dragon and its unique situation. Loved the innovations. Appreciated the masterminding, though would have liked more iron in that velvet glove. There is a good future possible, now. Can't wait for the last of the trilogy. <br /><br />Favorite quote:<b>
  <blockquote>All you need is a little help, same as me,” Jaxom was crying, pounding at the crack with his fists.</blockquote>
</b></span>

<div id="review_254329497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254329497" />
    <a title="Ricky Ganci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5628971-ricky-ganci"><img alt="Ricky Ganci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589290938p2/5628971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254329497?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricky Ganci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricky Ganci" href="/user/show/5628971-ricky-ganci">Ricky Ganci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254329497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer657141371834896699">Jumping ahead 7 Turns, I felt like this book settled me into the continued plot very comfortably. She became a bit longer-winded in this volume, spending a bit more time with character’s thoughts and reflections of events, but only once or twice did I feel distracted from the story and the danger of the Threadfall. F’nor takes a centerpiece in this novel, and it felt natural, being totally separate from the first book, which centered on F’lar and Lessa (both of whom appear in this book), who hav</span>
  <span id="freeText657141371834896699" style="display:none">Jumping ahead 7 Turns, I felt like this book settled me into the continued plot very comfortably. She became a bit longer-winded in this volume, spending a bit more time with character’s thoughts and reflections of events, but only once or twice did I feel distracted from the story and the danger of the Threadfall. F’nor takes a centerpiece in this novel, and it felt natural, being totally separate from the first book, which centered on F’lar and Lessa (both of whom appear in this book), who have settled in nicely to their role as dragonrider celebrities, so to speak. The conflict with the Oldtimers was a natural permutation of what would happen when people 400 years different attempt to do the same thing, and I was surprised at some of the sweet knife fights in these books. I was thinking I should really feel the absence of swordplay more in these books, but the way the world is set up really seems to not need swords and sorcery—more than a fantasy, these are works of hard science fiction, dealing with the colonization of planets and celestial occurrences. There are also some interesting themes dealing with human history and the propensity to forget useful, helpful, and even necessary things, with a hint of critique on what seemed like revisionist history—the value of the grubs being totally forgotten and overlooked. It was pretty good, though I missed the “training” scenes from the previous book. I want to ride a dragon—maybe a white one? I’m glad that the third book deals with that aspect of the story—a white dragon sounds awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="657141371834896699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_327867295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/327867295" />
    <a title="Marie Malyon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7512050-marie-malyon"><img alt="Marie Malyon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327358695p2/7512050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/327867295?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marie Malyon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marie Malyon" href="/user/show/7512050-marie-malyon">Marie Malyon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552116350" href="/book/show/949116.Dragonquest">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer327867295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8785727795213190741">I was lent this book along with nine others in the series by a good friend along with the recommendation they are his favourite fantasy books. I have to say now that I am at the second in the series I have not been let down.<br/><br/>Don't let the publication date of 1971 put you off! This has some seriously well developed female characters of Lessa, Kylara & Brekke who I fell in love with in this book. The developing relationships, emotional turmoils and childhood scandals appealed to me greatly and I lo</span>
  <span id="freeText8785727795213190741" style="display:none">I was lent this book along with nine others in the series by a good friend along with the recommendation they are his favourite fantasy books. I have to say now that I am at the second in the series I have not been let down.<br /><br />Don't let the publication date of 1971 put you off! This has some seriously well developed female characters of Lessa, Kylara &amp; Brekke who I fell in love with in this book. The developing relationships, emotional turmoils and childhood scandals appealed to me greatly and I love to read how they unfolded.<br /><br />The narrative although complete fantasy comes to life with the political conflicts and the breaking of social customs being easy to relate to even today. The tension between Bender Weyr and the 'Old Timers' seems tangable and believable and the discoveries about the ancients, as well as the future are so well written I often get carried away into their world and forgot that I was living in the weyr.<br /><br />My main criticism still stands, that the vast number of characters, places and dragon names all become very confusing and I found myself using the helpful little guide at the back more than once. The map at the front is also very helpful to track the characters across Pern as they fly between.<br /><br />Recommended to all lovers of fantasy, can wait to read the next one!!<br /><br />P.S. If any one finds a fire lizard egg please let me have one!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8785727795213190741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_570809846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570809846" />
    <a title="Juushika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/616321-juushika"><img alt="Juushika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541586729p2/616321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570809846?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juushika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juushika" href="/user/show/616321-juushika">Juushika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=status-borrowed">status-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=trope-companion-animal">trope-companion-animal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570809846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer614174636678795390">When Thread begins to fall out of schedule Pern is thrown into high agitation, aggravating troubled political relationships and sending dragonriders on a new quest: to stop the threat of Thread for good. For such a bold aim, <i>Dragonquest</i> is markedly undirected. It discards the flawed but compelling POVs of <i>Dragonflight</i> and replaces them with an ensemble cast, headhopping, and a pair of inspired minor protagonists. While largely political the plot lacks politicking (McCaffrey's antagonists are pro</span>
  <span id="freeText614174636678795390" style="display:none">When Thread begins to fall out of schedule Pern is thrown into high agitation, aggravating troubled political relationships and sending dragonriders on a new quest: to stop the threat of Thread for good. For such a bold aim, <i>Dragonquest</i> is markedly undirected. It discards the flawed but compelling POVs of <i>Dragonflight</i> and replaces them with an ensemble cast, headhopping, and a pair of inspired minor protagonists. While largely political the plot lacks politicking (McCaffrey's antagonists are problematically characterized--there's a disgusting amount of slut-shaming--and blatantly wrong), the pacing is poor, and there's almost no "quest" to speak of: characters themselves admit that the solution to their problem is uninspiring and disappointingly mundane. At times, Pern is an interesting place--the lingering impact of the technologically advanced society that founded it is especially intriguing, and the dragons remain appealing although their newly-introduced miniature cousins bring little to the story. But McCaffrey's worldbuilding is heavyhanded, her writing clunky, and what little good the book has fails to save it from its plentiful flaws. I didn't enjoy <i>Dragonquest</i> and don't recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="614174636678795390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3799351-don-bradshaw?shelf=m-f-romance">m-f-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1073708521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10323115686616748925"> Buddy read with Vivian.<br/> This installment was much more political with less thread fighting as some major changes are made on Pern. F'lar has always been a leader but tried to give the leadership over all away but was forced to take it. Somehow F'lar as been cast as the bad guy in some reader's minds because he tends to hold his cards close to his chest. If the poor guy shared most of his thoughts of his imagined future for Pern he would have a revolution on his hands. There were some amazing di</span>
  <span id="freeText10323115686616748925" style="display:none"> Buddy read with Vivian.<br /> This installment was much more political with less thread fighting as some major changes are made on Pern. F'lar has always been a leader but tried to give the leadership over all away but was forced to take it. Somehow F'lar as been cast as the bad guy in some reader's minds because he tends to hold his cards close to his chest. If the poor guy shared most of his thoughts of his imagined future for Pern he would have a revolution on his hands. There were some amazing discoveries made when Jaxom and Felessan were sneaking around the old caverns. Many instruments that the ancients had stored away got everyone excited. I love the Master Craftmen and was happy to see them beginning to share knowledge. Pern under F'lar is slowly becoming more open. These new happenings were tempered by sadness and heart ache that could have been avoided if some egos were not over inflated. I think some of the parties involved needed to die but that just my opinion. A white dragon was hatched from Ramoth's last clutch which was an unprecedented first in the histories. Changes are coming to Pern but will the people accept them? </span>
  <a data-text-id="10323115686616748925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1402058947" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3998317724841759668">I still love this book for what it is and for what it sets up. At the same time, I was totally bowled over by a certain dubious consent scene and other attitudes legitimising domestic violence that weren't part of my awareness when I first read these books (many times) as a teenager. They alter my fondness for a character I otherwise like very much and a relationship that I always viewed very positively. Disappointing. The words might not change, but times and attitudes do. A fascinating way to </span>
  <span id="freeText3998317724841759668" style="display:none">I still love this book for what it is and for what it sets up. At the same time, I was totally bowled over by a certain dubious consent scene and other attitudes legitimising domestic violence that weren't part of my awareness when I first read these books (many times) as a teenager. They alter my fondness for a character I otherwise like very much and a relationship that I always viewed very positively. Disappointing. The words might not change, but times and attitudes do. A fascinating way to measure the development of my own thinking and my consciousness of social issues as my horizons have broadened over the years. Anne McCaffrey proved herself to be a bit of an Oldtimer herself here. For a relatively feminist and obliquely gay-friendly world, some nuances of its culture are still quite dated. <br /><br />Having said that, DRAGONS. FIRE LIZARDS. AMBITIOUS PLOT. DRAGONS. TRADITION vs. INNOVATION. DRAGONS. RUTH &lt;3 Ultimately, the core Pern books champion moving away from dated attitudes to more enlightened, civilised ideals, methods, technologies and social systems, so they'll always have that trend in their favour.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3998317724841759668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25906613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4641352256756399531">Initial impression: So far, slower and more boring than the first, with more traditional gender roles.<br/><br/>Final conclusion: It seems like maybe Anne McCaffrey had nothing going on so she decided to try to write a follow-up to Dragonflight, but when she started, she couldn't figure out what to write about. Not much happens in this book-- really just a bunch of boring arguing. Some of the times/dates are off, with certain characters being too young or too old to mesh with what did/didn't happen in the</span>
  <span id="freeText4641352256756399531" style="display:none">Initial impression: So far, slower and more boring than the first, with more traditional gender roles.<br /><br />Final conclusion: It seems like maybe Anne McCaffrey had nothing going on so she decided to try to write a follow-up to Dragonflight, but when she started, she couldn't figure out what to write about. Not much happens in this book-- really just a bunch of boring arguing. Some of the times/dates are off, with certain characters being too young or too old to mesh with what did/didn't happen in the first book. It's a slower read, and the characters aren't particularly compelling either. Most disappointing of all is the complete role reversal of Lessa, who in the first book was a strong woman. In this book, she's a typical "helpmeet," no longer strong or powerful . . . or interesting. In book one, she was a woman, but in this book, she and most other women are almost always referred to as "girls." <br /><br />So much sci-fi is so unimaginative and boring when authors repeat the same tired gender stereotypes. Crash and burn, McCaffrey!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4641352256756399531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10296585261796369049" style="display:none">It's been too long since I first read Dragonflight so I don't remember very much except that I thoroughly enjoyed it. So I did find the first couple of chapters a bit of a struggle just getting back into this world; all the characters and special words etc but once I was past that, I was flying through the novel.<br /><br />Dragonquest is a novel filled with fun &amp; interesting characters (including the dragons) and even if it's more political than I never thought it could be, this was an enjoyable turn to the novel. They may have averted disaster in the last book but it was not the ending of all their troubles. This time, with progress and discoveries, they look for a more permanent solution.<br /><br />I would have given more stars except that I felt the ending was just too rushed and a bit rear-ended to squish into the average size book (?) Not sure but I just felt it didn't end well for me. And I still have questions... whether these are answered in the rest of the series/chronicles, who know...</span>

    <a title="Deborah Ideiosepius" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius"><img alt="Deborah Ideiosepius" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425943228p2/4802663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2038724272?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Ideiosepius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Ideiosepius" href="/user/show/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius">Deborah Ideiosepius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780853911913" href="/book/show/2490184.Dragonquest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=2017-reading-challenge">2017-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038724272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8584145774467653063">This is the second of the dragonriders of Pern book, not chronologically but in order of publication. This is a far more important order in my estimation, since the later written books lacked the creativity of the early ones.<br/><br/>Dragonquest is set seven years after Dragonflight was but was published a mere two years after the first book. The characters are continued from the first book with relatively few changes. Lessa, F'lar, F'nor are all pretty much the same and the Masterharper and Mastersmith </span>
  <span id="freeText8584145774467653063" style="display:none">This is the second of the dragonriders of Pern book, not chronologically but in order of publication. This is a far more important order in my estimation, since the later written books lacked the creativity of the early ones.<br /><br />Dragonquest is set seven years after Dragonflight was but was published a mere two years after the first book. The characters are continued from the first book with relatively few changes. Lessa, F'lar, F'nor are all pretty much the same and the Masterharper and Mastersmith continue to play their parts. This book covers the acrimonious split which occurred between the oldtimer dragon riders that Lessa brought forward to save Pern. It also covers the first impressions of fire-lizards and their introduction to the notice of Pernese.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this book, but it would not at all suit anyone who had not read Dragonflight recently. In writing style McCaffrey was way ahead of her time with this one; the current fashion of having a fantasy book completely reliant upon previous books is evident here. The early parts of the book are tense; McCaffrey is setting us up for all the difficulties, tensions and social issues that the story is addressing. There are a lot of them, so there is a fair bit of uncomfortable reading early in the book, it takes a while to get into is what I am suggesting.<br /><br />As always, the true charm for me with McCaffreys early books (well, aside from the lovely world building, the charming fiction, the good characters and the nice writing style) is the level of social commentary that is incorporated into the fictional story. In Quest, she looks at tradition vs innovation and how changes can affect people who are unprepared for change.Some of the points she makes remind me of Alvin Toffler and his book Future Shock, which examines peoples ability to cope with technological changes. In Pern, there is no technology as we know it, but the Weyrs are simultaneously trying to recover lost knowledge and techniques, and invent new solutions.<br /><br />Now for one of my normal 'old book warnings'. This book was copyrighted in 1971. Think about that: That was the year the very first e-book was posted (the origin of the Gutenberg project) Australian troops withdrew from America's war in Vietnam. Jim Morrison, The Doors lead singer died.... What I am saying was that this was a different world and from some of the reviews I have read, many readers don't get that.<br /><br />One reader complained that the romance was disgusting because it talks about a man 'overcoming the resistance' of a woman. Granted, that is nasty by 2000's standards, if that will bother you significantly, maybe skip this one. But it is small and understated (as is all the romance section in this book) and if you think you can grimace and bear it for a second or two, try the book anyway. If you think that is bad though, try reading a few of the Mills and Boons or bodice rippers written in the 70's - you will be horrified, rape used to be thought completely ok in romance novels.<br /><br />Another said they thought it might be racist. That one really left me scratching my head; McCaffrey never really mentions race at all and I suspect that is intentional. I once read an interview with her where she said that she purposefully made NO religion AT ALL in the Pern books. She considered religion to have messed up society badly and she wanted to create a society free of it. Given that America in the 70's had horrible racial problems, I would not be surprised if she had intentionally eliminated race as well as religion.<br /><br />In any case, this is a good book, if you enjoyed Dragonflight it is well worth going on to read this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8584145774467653063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46987808?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara ★" href="/user/show/1968285-barbara">Barbara ★</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968285-barbara?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968285-barbara?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968285-barbara?shelf=zzcover-white">zzcover-white</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968285-barbara?shelf=paranormal-dragons">paranormal-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968285-barbara?shelf=aliens-space">aliens-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968285-barbara?shelf=zzz-cover-fire">zzz-cover-fire</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46987808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1487361530236503451">I've been very reluctant to continue this series though I did try a month or so ago to read Dragonquest and was so darn confused that I gave up on it. I need it for a challenge so decided to give it another try. Again it's very confusing but I'm determined to read it this time since I've already committed to White Dragon for August. Hopefully I'll be able to stomach another one.<br/><br/>Like the first book, this has a very slow start that takes a good 100 pages before everything began to make sense and I</span>
  <span id="freeText1487361530236503451" style="display:none">I've been very reluctant to continue this series though I did try a month or so ago to read Dragonquest and was so darn confused that I gave up on it. I need it for a challenge so decided to give it another try. Again it's very confusing but I'm determined to read it this time since I've already committed to White Dragon for August. Hopefully I'll be able to stomach another one.<br /><br />Like the first book, this has a very slow start that takes a good 100 pages before everything began to make sense and I became invested in the story. I was interested in how they were finding new ways to defeat the Threads; Brekke and T'Nor's romance; Jaxom's impressing a dragon and what they were going to do with Kylara (that bitch). <br /><br />The only real issue I had with the book was the rape scene. It's one thing when it's necessitated by the dragon's heat and unavoidable but this was pure rape.<br /><br />p.161 "He wanted to be gentle but, unaccountably B fought him. <i>(She was a virgin after all.)</i> She pleaded with him, crying out wildly. He wasn't gentle but he was thorough, and in the end, B astounded him with a surrender as passionate as if her dragon was involved." Well that makes it all right then. NOT!<br /></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('28uFpdRqZ+EHLKPZ8QqeOhaOsOzmqQeo1wLm5SVyLSCj0/pJL1OM3jDc/Shv08dQT/1YffCYvjueVYo6LckSSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AhGedXPGnDuQi34SuoOSzCd1AnFoXxqvDikM6FIyVsV6CeGZiP93BKd7IOMkWsumfgbq4H5uozxHfmA3Wolprw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Somehow, Lorana must find a cure before the dragons-including her own beloved Arith-succumb to the sickness, leaving Pern undefended. The lyrics of an all-but-forgotten song seem to point toward an answer from nearly five hundred years in the past, when Kitti Ping and her daughter Wind Blossom bred the first dragons from their smaller cousins, the fire-lizards. No doubt the first colonists possessed the advanced technology to find the cure for which Lorana seeks, but over the centuries, that knowledge has been lost. Or has it? For in the distant past, an aged Wind Blossom worries that the germs that affect the fire-lizards may one day turn on larger prey-and unleash a plague that will destroy the dragons, Pern\'s only defenders against Thread. But as her people struggle to survive, Wind Blossom has neither the time nor the resources to expend on a future that may never arrive-until suddenly sheuncovers evidence that her worst fears will come true. Now two brave women, separated by hundreds of years but joined by bonds transcending time, will become unknowing allies in a desperate race against sickness and Threadfall, with nothing less than the survival of all life on Pern at stake. As the author of the &quot;Dragonriders of Pern&quot; series, McCaffrey (b. 1926) was one of the most significant writers of science fiction and fantasy. She was the first woman to win the Hugo and Nebula awards, and her 1978 novel &quot;The White Dragon&quot; was the first science-fiction novel to appear on the New York Times hardcover bestseller list. \n\nThis biography reveals a fascinating and complex figure, one who created and re-created her fiction by drawing on life experiences. At various stages, McCaffrey was a beautiful young girl who refused to fit into traditional gender roles in high school, a restless young mother who wanted to write, an American expatriate who became an Irish citizen, an animal lover who dreamed of fantasy worlds with perfect relationships between humans and beasts, and a wife trapped in an unhappy marriage just as the women\'s movement took hold. \n\nAuthor Robin Roberts conducted interviews with McCaffrey, her children, friends, and colleagues, and used archival correspondence and contemporary reviews and criticism. The biography examines how McCaffrey\'s early interests in theater, Slavonic languages and literature, and British history, mythology, and culture all shaped her science fiction. The book is a nuanced portrait of a writer whose appeal extends well beyond readers of her chosen genre.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13394980384758597677\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">About Anne McCaffrey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1599324585p3/26.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">Anne McCaffrey
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10724646126976677297">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br/><br/>Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText10724646126976677297" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />She died at the age of 85, after suffering a massive stroke on 21 November 2011.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a>, <a href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826" rel="nofollow noopener">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10724646126976677297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
